## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a core problem in materials science and solid mechanics. Stress typically increases with strain through elastic/plastic mechanisms and decreases with temperature due to thermal softening.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic stress-strain curve)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Hollomon with Arrhenius thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T**(-1)) (thermally activated plastic flow)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress and hardening)
- Ludwik with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (yield + hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (c3 + c4 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Swift model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)
- Swift with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (pre-strained power law with thermal activation)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (quadratic strain with cross-coupling)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) * (c3 - c4 * T) (nonlinear with saturation and thermal softening)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T**(-1))) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress expression (c0 + f(epsilon)) representing initial yield before hardening
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 - c1*T) on stress, reflecting modulus decrease with temperature
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius factor exp(c / T) multiplying strain-dependent terms, from dislocation glide activation energy
- Pre-strain or initial dislocation density → Offset in strain argument (epsilon + c0)**n rather than epsilon**n alone
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as ratio or shifted form (T - c0) representing distance from reference/melting temperature
- Competing hardening and recovery → Difference of power-law and linear terms: c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*epsilon, representing work hardening vs dynamic recovery
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product term epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 representing enhanced thermal softening at higher strains
